<p><i><b>Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace</b></i> is a 1999 American <a href="/wiki/Epic_film" title="Epic film">epic</a> <a href="/wiki/Space_opera" title="Space opera">space opera</a> film written and directed by <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a>. It is the fourth film in the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> saga to be released, the first of a three-part <a href="/wiki/Prequel" title="Prequel">prequel</a> to the original <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy, and the first film in the story chronology. The film was Lucas' first production as a film director after a 22-year hiatus following <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">the original <i>Star Wars</i> film</a>, and his fourth film overall.</p>
<p>The film's narrative follows the <a href="/wiki/Jedi" title="Jedi">Jedi Knight</a> <a href="/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn" title="Qui-Gon Jinn">Qui-Gon Jinn</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Apprenticeship" title="Apprenticeship">apprentice</a> <a href="/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi" title="Obi-Wan Kenobi">Obi-Wan Kenobi</a>. They escort and protect <a href="/wiki/Padm%C3%A9_Amidala" title="Padmé Amidala">Queen Amidala</a>, who is traveling from the planet <a href="/wiki/Naboo" title="Naboo">Naboo</a> to the planet <a href="/wiki/Coruscant" title="Coruscant">Coruscant</a>, hoping to find a peaceful end to a large-scale interplanetary trade dispute. The story also features a young <a href="/wiki/Darth_Vader" title="Darth Vader">Anakin Skywalker</a> before he became a Jedi; he is introduced as a young slave boy who appears to have unusually strong nascent powers of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Force_(Star_Wars)" title="Force (Star Wars)">the Force</a> and must contend with the mysterious return of the <a href="/wiki/Sith" title="Sith">Sith</a>.</p>
<p>Lucas began production of this film after he concluded that film <a href="/wiki/Special_effect" title="Special effect">special effects</a> had advanced to the level he wanted for the fourth film in the saga. Filming started on June 26, 1997, at locations including <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Studios,_Leavesden" title="Warner Bros. Studios, Leavesden">Leavesden Film Studios</a> and the Tunisian desert. Its visual effects included extensive use of <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> (CGI); some of its characters and settings were completely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_computing_1950%E2%80%931979" title="Timeline of computing 1950–1979">computerized</a> and did not exist in the real world.</p>
<p><i>Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace</i> premiered in theaters on May 19, 1999; sixteen years after the premiere of the previous <i>Star Wars</i> film, <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i>. The film's premiere was extensively covered by media and was greatly anticipated because of the large cultural following the <i>Star Wars</i> saga had cultivated. Despite mixed reviews by critics, who tended to praise the visuals and action sequences but criticized the writing, characterization and acting, it grossed more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$924.3 million</span> worldwide during its initial theatrical run, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">second-highest-grossing film</a> worldwide at the time—behind <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>. It became the highest-grossing film of 1999, the highest-grossing <i>Star Wars</i> film, and is currently the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">fifth-highest-grossing film in North America</a> unadjusted for inflation. A 3D reissue, which has earned an additional <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$102.7 million</span> at the box office and brought the film's overall worldwide takings to over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1 billion</span>, was released in February 2012.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In response to taxation on trade routes in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galactic_Republic_(Star_Wars)" title="Galactic Republic (Star Wars)">Galactic Republic</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Trade_Federation" title="Trade Federation">Trade Federation</a> organizes a blockade of battleships around the planet <a href="/wiki/Naboo" title="Naboo">Naboo</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Chancellor_Valorum" title="Supreme Chancellor Valorum">Supreme Chancellor Valorum</a> dispatches <a href="/wiki/Jedi" title="Jedi">Jedi Master</a> <a href="/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn" title="Qui-Gon Jinn">Qui-Gon Jinn</a> and his apprentice <a href="/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi" title="Obi-Wan Kenobi">Obi-Wan Kenobi</a> to negotiate with the Trade Federation leadership to end the blockade. <a href="/wiki/Palpatine" title="Palpatine">Darth Sidious</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Sith" title="Sith">Sith Lord</a> and the Trade Federation's secret adviser, orders Federation Viceroy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nute_Gunray" title="Nute Gunray">Nute Gunray</a> to kill the Jedi and invade Naboo with an army of <a href="/wiki/Battle_droid" title="Battle droid">battle droids</a>. The Jedi flee to Naboo, where Qui-Gon saves <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gungan" title="Gungan">Gungan</a> outcast <a href="/wiki/Jar_Jar_Binks" title="Jar Jar Binks">Jar Jar Binks</a> from being killed during the invasion. Indebted to the Jedi, Jar Jar leads them to an underwater Gungan city. There the Jedi try but fail to persuade the Gungan leader, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boss_Nass" title="Boss Nass">Boss Nass</a> into helping the people of Naboo, though they are able to obtain transportation to Theed, the capital city on the surface. They rescue <a href="/wiki/Padm%C3%A9_Amidala" title="Padmé Amidala">Queen Amidala</a>, the ruler of the Naboo people, and escape the planet on her royal starship, which is damaged as they pass the Federation blockade.</p>
<p>Amidala's ship is unable to sustain its <a href="/wiki/Hyperdrive" title="Hyperdrive">hyperdrive</a> and lands for repairs on the desert planet <a href="/wiki/Tatooine" title="Tatooine">Tatooine</a>. Qui-Gon, Jar Jar, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astromech_droid" title="Astromech droid">astromech droid</a> <a href="/wiki/R2-D2" title="R2-D2">R2-D2</a>, and Amidala's handmaiden Padmé visit the settlement of Mos Espa to buy new parts at a junk shop. There they meet the shop's owner <a href="/wiki/Watto" title="Watto">Watto</a> and his nine-year-old slave <a href="/wiki/Darth_Vader" title="Darth Vader">Anakin Skywalker</a>, who is a gifted <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Podracer" title="Podracer">Podracer</a> pilot and engineer, and has created a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protocol_droid" title="Protocol droid">protocol droid</a> called <a href="/wiki/C-3PO" title="C-3PO">C-3PO</a>. Qui-Gon senses a strong presence of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Force_(Star_Wars)" title="Force (Star Wars)">Force</a> within Anakin and is convinced that he is the "chosen one" of Jedi prophecy who will bring balance to the Force. Qui-Gon wagers Anakin's freedom with Watto in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Podrace" title="Podrace">Podrace</a>, which Anakin wins. Anakin joins the group to be trained as a Jedi, leaving his mother <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shmi_Skywalker" title="Shmi Skywalker">Shmi</a> behind. En route to their repaired starship, Qui-Gon enters a brief <a href="/wiki/Lightsaber" title="Lightsaber">lightsaber</a> duel with <a href="/wiki/Darth_Maul" title="Darth Maul">Darth Maul</a>, Darth Sidious' Sith apprentice who was sent to capture Amidala.</p>
<p>The Jedi escort Amidala to the Republic capital planet <a href="/wiki/Coruscant" title="Coruscant">Coruscant</a> so she can plead her people's case to Chancellor Valorum in the Galactic Senate. Qui-Gon asks the <a href="/wiki/Jedi_Council" title="Jedi Council">Jedi Council</a> to train Anakin as a Jedi, but the Council are concerned that Anakin is vulnerable to the <a href="/wiki/Dark_side_(Star_Wars)" title="Dark side (Star Wars)">dark side of the Force</a> and decline. Undaunted, Qui-Gon vows to train Anakin himself. Meanwhile, Naboo senator <a href="/wiki/Palpatine" title="Palpatine">Palpatine</a> persuades Amidala to make a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vote_of_no_confidence" title="Vote of no confidence">vote of no confidence</a> in Valorum to elect a more capable chancellor to resolve the crisis on Naboo. Though she pushes for the vote, Amidala grows frustrated with the corruption in the Senate and decides to return to Naboo with the Jedi.</p>
<p>On Naboo, Padmé reveals herself to the Gungans as Queen Amidala and persuades them into an alliance against the Trade Federation. Jar Jar leads his people in a battle against the droid army while Padmé leads the hunt for Gunray in Theed, eventually capturing him and his aide, Rune Haako. In a starship hangar, Anakin enters a vacant starfighter and inadvertently triggers its <a href="/wiki/Autopilot" title="Autopilot">autopilot</a>, joining the battle against the Federation droid control ship in space. Anakin ventures into the ship and destroys it from within, deactivating the droid army. Meanwhile, Qui-Gon and Obi-Wan battle Darth Maul, who mortally wounds Qui-Gon before being bisected by Obi-Wan. As he dies, Qui-Gon asks Obi-Wan to train Anakin. Subsequently, Palpatine is elected as the new Supreme Chancellor and Gunray and is formally arrested. The Jedi Council makes Obi-Wan a fully fledged Jedi Knight and reluctantly accepts Anakin as Obi-Wan's apprentice. At a festive ceremony, Padmé presents a gift of appreciation and friendship to the Gungans.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anakinyoung.jpg"><img alt="A blonde boy wearing a gray robe and a black backpack walks in a desert." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="276" data-file-width="222" height="211" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Anakinyoung.jpg/170px-Anakinyoung.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/4a/Anakinyoung.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/4a/Anakinyoung.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anakinyoung.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jake_Lloyd" title="Jake Lloyd">Jake Lloyd</a> portrayed 9-year-old Anakin Skywalker.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Liam_Neeson" title="Liam Neeson">Liam Neeson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Qui-Gon_Jinn" title="Qui-Gon Jinn">Qui-Gon Jinn</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Jedi" title="Jedi">Jedi Master</a> and mentor to Obi-Wan. When he discovers Anakin he insists that the boy be trained as a Jedi despite the Jedi Council's protests. Lucas originally wanted to cast an American actor in the role, but cast Irishman Neeson because he considered that Neeson had great skills and presence. Lucas said Neeson was a "master actor, who the other actors will look up to, who has got the qualities of strength that the character demands".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ewan_McGregor" title="Ewan McGregor">Ewan McGregor</a> as <a href="/wiki/Obi-Wan_Kenobi" title="Obi-Wan Kenobi">Obi-Wan Kenobi</a>, Qui-Gon's young Jedi apprentice. He holds Qui-Gon in high regard but questions his motives at times. McGregor was cast from a shortlist of fifty actors, all of whom had to be compared to pictures of young <a href="/wiki/Alec_Guinness" title="Alec Guinness">Alec Guinness</a>, who portrayed the elderly Obi-Wan, to make a believable younger version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199944-45_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199944-45-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> McGregor had a vocal coach to help his voice sound closer to Guinness'. He also studied several of Guinness' performances, from his early work and the <i>Star Wars</i> movies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Natalie_Portman" title="Natalie Portman">Natalie Portman</a> as <a href="/wiki/Padm%C3%A9_Amidala" title="Padmé Amidala">Queen Padmé Amidala</a>: Amidala, the 14-year-old Queen of Naboo, hopes to protect her planet from a blockade by the Trade Federation. Over 200 actors auditioned for the role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> The Production notes stated; "The role required a young woman who could be believable as the ruler of that planet, but at the same time be vulnerable and open". Portman was chosen especially for her performances in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_(film)" title="Léon (film)">The Professional</a></i> (1994) and <i><a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Girls_(film)" title="Beautiful Girls (film)">Beautiful Girls</a></i> (1996), which impressed Lucas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> He stated, "I was looking for someone who was young, strong, along the lines of <a href="/wiki/Princess_Leia" title="Princess Leia">Leia</a> [and] Natalie embodied all those traits and more".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> Portman was unfamiliar with <i>Star Wars</i> before being cast,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> but was enthusiastic about being cast as a character she expected to become a role model. Portman said, "It was wonderful playing a young queen with so much power. I think it will be good for young women to see a strong woman of action who is also smart and a leader."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ian_McDiarmid" title="Ian McDiarmid">Ian McDiarmid</a> as <a href="/wiki/Palpatine" title="Palpatine">Senator/Chancellor Palpatine / Darth Sidious</a>, a Senator of Naboo who is eventually elected Chancellor of the Republic. McDiarmid was surprised when Lucas approached him 16 years after <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i> to reprise the role of Palpatine because he had assumed that a younger actor would play the part in the prequel films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jake_Lloyd" title="Jake Lloyd">Jake Lloyd</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anakin_Skywalker" title="Anakin Skywalker">Anakin Skywalker</a>, a nine-year-old slave boy and a skilled pilot who dreams of becoming a Jedi. Hundreds of actors were tested<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ProductionNotes_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-ProductionNotes-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> before the producers settled on Lloyd, who Lucas considered met his requirements of "a good actor, enthusiastic and very energetic". Producer <a href="/wiki/Rick_McCallum" title="Rick McCallum">Rick McCallum</a> said that Lloyd was "smart, mischievous and loves anything mechanical—just like Anakin".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NotesII_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-NotesII-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pernilla_August" title="Pernilla August">Pernilla August</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shmi_Skywalker" title="Shmi Skywalker">Shmi Skywalker</a>, Anakin's mother who is concerned for her son's future and allows him leave with the Jedi. August, a veteran of Swedish cinema, was chosen after auditioning with Liam Neeson. She was afraid of being rejected because of her accent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-behind_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-behind-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Best" title="Ahmed Best">Ahmed Best</a> as <a href="/wiki/Jar_Jar_Binks" title="Jar Jar Binks">Jar Jar Binks</a>, a clumsy <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Star_Wars_races_(F-J)#Gungan" title="List of Star Wars races (F-J)">Gungan</a>, exiled from his home and taken in by Qui-Gon and Obi-Wan. He accompanies them throughout the film. Best was hired after Gurland saw him on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stomp_(dance_troupe)" title="Stomp (dance troupe)">Stomp</a> performance in San Francisco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NotesII_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-NotesII-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Best was originally intended to provide motion capture data but his offer to voice the character was accepted. On the set, to provide references for the actors, Best was clothed in a suit made of foam and latex and a headpiece. Best's filmed performance was later replaced with the computer-generated character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-behind_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-behind-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Best frequently improvised movements to make Jar Jar look as clumsy and comedic as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NotesII_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-NotesII-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ray_Park" title="Ray Park">Ray Park</a> as <a href="/wiki/Darth_Maul" title="Darth Maul">Darth Maul</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Star_Wars_races_(U-Z)#Zabrak" title="List of Star Wars races (U-Z)">Zabrak</a> and Darth Sidious' Sith apprentice who uses a double-bladed lightsaber. A <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts" title="Martial arts">martial arts</a> champion with experience in gymnastics and swordfighting, Park was originally a member of the stunt crew.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NotesII_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-NotesII-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Stunt coordinator <a href="/wiki/Nick_Gillard" title="Nick Gillard">Nick Gillard</a> filmed Park to demonstrate his conception of the lightsaber battles. Lucas and McCallum were so impressed with the test tape that they gave Park the role of Maul. His voice was considered "too squeaky" and was dubbed over.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-behind_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-behind-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> He was voiced by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Serafinowicz" title="Peter Serafinowicz">Peter Serafinowicz</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Anthony_Daniels" title="Anthony Daniels">Anthony Daniels</a> voices <a href="/wiki/C-3PO" title="C-3PO">C-3PO</a>, a protocol droid built by Anakin. It lacks a metal covering in this film; R2-D2 refers to it as being "naked". A puppeteer dressed in a color closely matching the background—in a manner similar to the Japanese puppet theater <a href="/wiki/Bunraku" title="Bunraku">Bunraku</a>—manipulated a skeletal C-3PO figure attached to his front while Daniels read his lines off-camera. The puppeteer was erased from the film during post-production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NotesII_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-NotesII-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kenny_Baker_(English_actor)" title="Kenny Baker (English actor)">Kenny Baker</a> as <a href="/wiki/R2-D2" title="R2-D2">R2-D2</a>, an astromech droid that saves Queen Amidala's ship when other droids fail. Before the film's production started, fans campaigned on the Internet to retain Baker as R2-D2; Lucas replied that the actor would remain. Baker is used for scenes where R2-D2 bends forwards and backwards and wobbles from side to side. Robots and a digital replica were used in other shots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Silas_Carson" title="Silas Carson">Silas Carson</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nute_Gunray" title="Nute Gunray">Nute Gunray</a>, the Viceroy of the Trade Federation who leads Naboo's invasion and tries to force Queen Amidala to sign a treaty to legitimize the occupation. Carson also portrays three minor characters: Jedi Master <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ki-Adi-Mundi" title="Ki-Adi-Mundi">Ki-Adi-Mundi</a>, Trade Federation Senator <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lott_Dod" title="Lott Dod">Lott Dod</a>, and an ill-fated pilot (the role Carson originally auditioned for).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Carson got the role because another actor was uncomfortable with the costumes used by the Trade Federation characters, which were hot, exerted a lot of pressure on the bearer, and took about 15 minutes to apply. Gunray's <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a> accent was chosen after Lucas and McCallum listened to various languages to decide how the Neimodians would speak.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hugh_Quarshie" title="Hugh Quarshie">Hugh Quarshie</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Captain_Panaka" title="Captain Panaka">Captain Panaka</a>, Queen Amidala's chief of security at Theed Palace. Quarshie considered the part "a good career move" and a production that would be fun to make.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frank_Oz" title="Frank Oz">Frank Oz</a> voices <a href="/wiki/Yoda" title="Yoda">Yoda</a>, the centuries-old leader of the Jedi Council who is apprehensive about allowing Anakin to be trained. Yoda was mostly portrayed as a puppet designed by <a href="/wiki/Nick_Dudman" title="Nick Dudman">Nick Dudman</a> based on <a href="/wiki/Stuart_Freeborn" title="Stuart Freeborn">Stuart Freeborn</a>'s original design. Oz controlled the puppet's mouth and other parts were controlled by puppeteers using remote controls.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-behind_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-behind-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Lucas fitted Yoda's filming around Oz's schedule as he finished and promoted <i><a href="/wiki/In_%26_Out" title="In &amp; Out">In &amp; Out</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199996_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199996-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> A computer-generated Yoda is featured in two distant shots. <a href="/wiki/Warwick_Davis" title="Warwick Davis">Warwick Davis</a> portrays him in the scene in which Obi-Wan becomes a Jedi Knight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Lucas said he originally wanted to use a full-time digital Yoda, but the attempts did not work well enough. On <i>The Phantom Menace</i> '​s Blu-ray version, which was also used for the 3D re-release, a CG Yoda similar to the one from the other prequels is used instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Samuel_L._Jackson" title="Samuel L. Jackson">Samuel L. Jackson</a> as <a href="/wiki/Mace_Windu" title="Mace Windu">Mace Windu</a>, member of the Jedi Council who also opposes the training of Anakin. After Jackson expressed interest in appearing in a <i>Star Wars</i> film, he was approached by cast director Robin Gurland to play Windu.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NotesII_7-5"><a href="#cite_note-NotesII-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Terence_Stamp" title="Terence Stamp">Terence Stamp</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Chancellor_Valorum" title="Supreme Chancellor Valorum">Supreme Chancellor Finis Valorum</a>, the current Chancellor who commissions Obi-Wan and Qui-Gon to negotiate with the Trade Federation Viceroy. Lucas described the character as a "good man but he's beleaguered—a bit like <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">[Bill] Clinton</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Oliver_Ford_Davies" title="Oliver Ford Davies">Oliver Ford Davies</a> as Sio Bibble, the governor of Naboo</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andy_Secombe" title="Andy Secombe">Andy Secombe</a> voices <a href="/wiki/Watto" title="Watto">Watto</a>, a junk dealer on Tatooine who owns Anakin and his mother as slaves. The character's design was an amalgam of rejected ideas; Watto's expressions were based on video footage of Secombe's voice acting, photographs of animation supervisor <a href="/wiki/Rob_Coleman" title="Rob Coleman">Rob Coleman</a> imitating the character, and modeler Steve Alpin saying Watto's lines to a mirror.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lewis_MacLeod_(actor)" title="Lewis MacLeod (actor)">Lewis MacLeod</a> voices <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sebulba" title="Sebulba">Sebulba</a>, an aggressive, scheming Podracer who is Anakin's rival. Lucas described Sebulba's design as "a spider crossed with an orangutan crossed with a sloth",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-time-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> with a camel-like face, and clothing inspired by medieval armor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brian_Blessed" title="Brian Blessed">Brian Blessed</a> voices <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boss_Nass" title="Boss Nass">Boss Nass</a>, the leader of the Gungan tribe who allies with the Naboo and defeats the Trade Federation. Blessed originally auditioned for the role of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sio_Bibble" title="Sio Bibble">Sio Bibble</a>, the Governor of Naboo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> for which he was considered "too loud".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blessed_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-blessed-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Casting director Robin Gurland approached him to play Nass because it was a "bigger than life" character with "a kind of bravado".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199951_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199951-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Blessed described Nass as a "reluctant hero",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-blessed_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-blessed-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> and a fun role to play.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greg_Proops" title="Greg Proops">Greg Proops</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Capurro" title="Scott Capurro">Scott Capurro</a> voice Fode and Beed, the two headed announcer of the Boonta's Eve Race. The actors were filmed wearing make-up and blue bodysuits so their heads could be joined in a computer-generated body. The visual effects crew did not like the original results and crafted Fode and Beed as an entirely computer generated alien.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sofia_Coppola" title="Sofia Coppola">Sofia Coppola</a> as Saché:,one of Amidala's handmaidens. Sofia, daughter of Lucas' long-time friend and creative partner <a href="/wiki/Francis_Ford_Coppola" title="Francis Ford Coppola">Francis Ford Coppola</a>, considers Lucas as "like an uncle to me". As she prepared the script for her directorial debut <i><a href="/wiki/The_Virgin_Suicides_(film)" title="The Virgin Suicides (film)">The Virgin Suicides</a></i>, Sofia heard Lucas would make a new <i>Star Wars</i> film and asked him if she could accompany him during filming. Lucas offered Coppola a role in the royal entourage, which she accepted because it "seemed like a good vantage point to watch without getting in the way".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ralph_Brown" title="Ralph Brown">Ralph Brown</a> as Ric Olié:, the Queen's starship pilot</li>
<li>Steven Speirs as Captain Tarpals, a Gungan general</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Keira_Knightley" title="Keira Knightley">Keira Knightley</a> as Sabé, one of Queen Amidala's handmaidens</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While he was writing <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">the original <i>Star Wars</i></a>, George Lucas reportedly realized the story he had written was too vast in scope to be covered in one film. The original film was intended to introduce a wider story arc that could be told in sequels if the first film was successful. <i>Star Wars</i> evolved from the first film in the sequence to a film belonging to the saga's second trilogy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> By the time of the third draft, Lucas had negotiated a contract that gave him rights to make two sequels. He had also developed an elaborate <a href="/wiki/Backstory" title="Backstory">backstory</a> to aid his writing process.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> While writing the first sequel, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Empire_Strikes_Back" title="The Empire Strikes Back">The Empire Strikes Back</a></i>, Lucas considered directions in which to take the story. He turned the villain Darth Vader into the father of hero <a href="/wiki/Luke_Skywalker" title="Luke Skywalker">Luke Skywalker</a> and developed a backstory in which Vader was once Jedi Knight Anakin Skywalker, a powerful warrior who defected to the dark side of the Force.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> With this backstory in place, Lucas decided the series would be a trilogy, renaming the film from "Episode II" to "Episode V".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> By the time of the trilogy's final film, <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i>, Vader became a tragic character and was ultimately redeemed. Lucas said he was "burned out" and would take a break from the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After losing much of his fortune in a divorce settlement in 1987, George Lucas had no desire to return to <i>Star Wars</i> and had unofficially canceled his <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_sequel_trilogy" title="Star Wars sequel trilogy">sequel trilogy</a> by the time of <i>Return of the Jedi</i>. Because Lucas had developed most of the backstory, the idea of prequels continued to fascinate him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> In the early 1990s, <i>Star Wars</i> saw a resurgence in popularity in the wake of <a href="/wiki/Dark_Horse_Comics" title="Dark Horse Comics">Dark Horse</a>'s <a href="/wiki/List_of_Star_Wars_comic_books" title="List of Star Wars comic books">comic line</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timothy_Zahn" title="Timothy Zahn">Timothy Zahn</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Thrawn_trilogy" title="Thrawn trilogy">trilogy of novels</a>. Lucas saw there was still a large audience for his idea of a prequel trilogy and with the development of special effects generated with <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> (CGI), Lucas considered returning to his saga and directing the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1993, it was announced in <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> and other sources that he would be making the prequels. Lucas began outlining the story; Anakin Skywalker rather than Obi-Wan Kenobi would be the main protagonist and the series would be a tragedy examining Darth Vader's origins. Lucas also began to change the prequels' timeline relative to the original series, "filling-in" the history, backstory, existing parallel or tangential to the originals and beginning a long story starting with Anakin's childhood and ended with his death. This was the final step towards turning the franchise into a saga.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>George Lucas began writing the new <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy on November 1, 1994.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idea_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Idea-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The screenplay of <i>Star Wars</i> was adapted from Lucas' 15-page outline that was written in 1976, which he designed to help him keep track of the characters' backstories and events that occurred before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_Wars_original_trilogy" title="Star Wars original trilogy">original trilogy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idea_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-Idea-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Anakin was first written as a twelve-year-old, but Lucas reduced his age to nine because he felt the lower age would fit better the plot point of Anakin being affected by his mother's separation from him. Eventually, Anakin's younger age led Lucas to rewrite his participation in the final battle, small scenes with him finding out how the ship works, and R2-D2 helping Anakin to make the story more believable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan19997_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan19997-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's working title was <i>The Beginning</i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Idea_36-2"><a href="#cite_note-Idea-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Lucas later revealed that its true title was <i>The Phantom Menace</i>; a reference to Palpatine hiding his true identity as an evil Sith Lord behind the facade of a well-intentioned public servant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The larger budget and possibilities opened up by the use of digital effects made Lucas "think about a much grander, more epic scale—which is what I wanted <i>Star Wars</i> to be".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vision_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-vision-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The story ended with five simultaneous, ongoing plots, one leading to another. The central plot is Palpatine's intent to become Chancellor, which leads to the Trade Federation's attack to Naboo, the Jedi being sent there, Anakin being met along the way, and the rise of the Sith Lords. As with the original trilogy, Lucas constructed <i>The Phantom Menace</i> to illustrate several themes through the narrative. Duality is a frequent theme; Amidala is a queen who passes as a handmaiden, Palpatine plays on both sides of the war, and Obi-Wan is in conflict with his rebellious master but eventually becomes Qui-Gon by confronting his rebellious personality and accepting his responsibilities. Balance is also frequently used; Anakin is supposedly the one chosen to bring balance to the Force and the characters have someone to influence them—Lucas said, "Anakin needed to have a mother, Obi-Wan needed a Master, Darth Sidious needed an apprentice" as without interaction and dialogue "you wouldn't have drama".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan19998.E2.80.939_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan19998.E2.80.939-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-production_and_design">Pre-production and design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pre-production and design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before Lucas had started writing, his producing partner <a href="/wiki/Rick_McCallum" title="Rick McCallum">Rick McCallum</a> was prepararing for the film. McCallum stated that his experience with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Young_Indiana_Jones_Chronicles" title="The Young Indiana Jones Chronicles">The Young Indiana Jones Chronicles</a></i> led to many of his decisions on <i>The Phantom Menace</i>, such as long-term deals with actors and soundstages, the employment of recent graduates with no film experience, and the creation of sets and landscapes with digital technology. In April 1994, McCallum started searching for artists in art, architecture and design schools, and in mid-year he began location scouting with production designer Gavin Bocquet. <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">Industrial Light &amp; Magic</a> (ILM) art director <a href="/wiki/Doug_Chiang" title="Doug Chiang">Doug Chiang</a> impressed McCallum the most and was hired as the design director.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199910.E2.80.9312_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199910.E2.80.9312-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Within three to four months of Lucas beginning the writing process, Chiang and his design team started a two-year process of reviewing thousands of designs for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Thousands_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Thousands-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Chiang stated that Lucas intended <i>Episode I</i> to be stylistically different from the other <i>Star Wars</i> films; it would be "richer and more like a period piece, since it was the history leading up to <i>A New Hope</i>". The three planets on which the story takes place—some with varied environments such as the human and Gungan cities of Naboo and three buildings in Coruscant. With the exception of the Gungan city, which had an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Art_nouveau" title="Art nouveau">art nouveau</a>-inspired visual, these locations would be given distinctive looks with some basis in the real world. The concept drawings of <a href="/wiki/Ralph_McQuarrie" title="Ralph McQuarrie">Ralph McQuarrie</a> for the original trilogy served as the basis for Mos Espa—which was also inspired by old Tunisian hotels and buildings and had touches such as a market place to differentiate it from <i>A New Hope</i> '​s Mos Eisley—and Coruscant, in particular a metropolis design which became the basis for the Senate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199912.E2.80.9317_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199912.E2.80.9317-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> Bocquet would later develop the work of Chiang's team and design the interiors, translating the concepts into construction blueprints with environments and architectural styles that had some basis in reality "to give the audience something to key into".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199954.E2.80.9355_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199954.E2.80.9355-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Some elements were directly inspired by the original trilogy; Lucas described the battle droids as predecessors to the <a href="/wiki/Stormtrooper_(Star_Wars)" title="Stormtrooper (Star Wars)">Stormtroopers</a>. Chiang uses that orientation to base the droids on the Imperial soldiers, only in the same style of stylized and elongated features seen in tribal African art.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vision_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-vision-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Terryl Whitlatch, who had a background on zoology and anatomy, was in charge of creature design. Many of the aliens are hybrids, combining features of real animals. At times entire food chains were developed even though only a small percentage of them would appear in the film. Whitlatch also designed detailed skeletons for the major characters and facial muscles on Jar Jar Binks as a reference for ILM's animators. Each creature would reflect its environment; those on Naboo were more beautiful because the planet is "lush and more animal-friendly", Tatooine has rough-looking creatures "with weather-beaten leathery skin to protect them from the harsh desert elements", and Coruscant has bipedal, human-looking aliens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199916.E2.80.9322_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199916.E2.80.9322-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Duel_of_the_Fates.jpg"><img alt="Three men fight with laser swords in an hangar." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="205" data-file-width="484" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ad/Duel_of_the_Fates.jpg/325px-Duel_of_the_Fates.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/ad/Duel_of_the_Fates.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/ad/Duel_of_the_Fates.jpg 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Duel_of_the_Fates.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Qui-Gon Jinn and Obi-Wan Kenobi dueling Darth Maul. Lucas wanted the lightsaber battles to be fast and more intense, depicting the Jedi in their prime.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stunt" title="Stunt">Stunt</a> coordinator <a href="/wiki/Nick_Gillard" title="Nick Gillard">Nick Gillard</a> was recruited to create a new Jedi fighting style for the prequel trilogy. Gillard likened the lightsaber battles to a chess game "with every move being a <a href="/wiki/Check_(chess)" title="Check (chess)">check</a>". Because of their short-range weapons, Gillard thought the Jedi would have had to develop a fighting style that merged every swordfighting style, such as <a href="/wiki/Kendo" title="Kendo">kendo</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Kenjutsu" title="Kenjutsu">kenjutsu</a> styles, with other swinging techniques, such as tennis swings and tree-chopping. While training Liam Neeson and Ewan McGregor, Gillard wrote a sequence which lasted around 60 seconds and intended to be around five or six sequences per fight.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prime_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prime-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Lucas later referred to the Jedi as "negotiators" rather than high-casualty soldiers. The preference of hand-to-hand combat was intended to give a spiritual and intellectual role to the Jedi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prime_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Prime-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> Because Gillard thought the stunt jumps with the actors and stuntmen dangling from wires did not look realistic, <a href="/wiki/Air_ram" title="Air ram">air rams</a> were used to propel them into the air instead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mak_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-mak-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lucas decided to make elaborate costumes because the film's society was more sophisticated than the one depicted in the original trilogy. Designer Trisha Biggar and her team created over 1,000 costumes that were inspired by various cultures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Biggar worked closely with concept designer Iain McCaig to create a color palette for the inhabitants of each world: Tatooine followed <i>A New Hope</i> with sun-bleached sand colors, Coruscant had grays, browns and blacks, and Naboo had green and gold for humans while Gungans wore "a leathery look, like their skin". The Jedi costumes followed the tradition from the original film;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199923_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199923-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Obi-Wan's costume was inspired by the costume that was worn by Guinness. Lucas said he and Biggar would look at the conceptual art to "translat[e] all of these designs into cloth and fabric and materials that would actually work and not look silly". Biggar also consulted Gillard to ensure the costumes would accommodate action scenes, and consulted the creature department to find which fabrics "wouldn't wear too heavily" on the alien skins. A huge wardrobe department was set up at <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Studios,_Leavesden" title="Warner Bros. Studios, Leavesden">Leavesden Film Studios</a> to create over 250 costumes for the main actors and 5,000 for the background ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199960.E2.80.9364_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199960.E2.80.9364-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Filming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Star_Wars_filming_locations" title="List of Star Wars filming locations">List of Star Wars filming locations</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Star_Wars_Episode_One_Village_-_05.jpg"><img alt="Rocky buildings and an antenna-like structure in a desert." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Star_Wars_Episode_One_Village_-_05.jpg/220px-Star_Wars_Episode_One_Village_-_05.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Star_Wars_Episode_One_Village_-_05.jpg/330px-Star_Wars_Episode_One_Village_-_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Star_Wars_Episode_One_Village_-_05.jpg/440px-Star_Wars_Episode_One_Village_-_05.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Star_Wars_Episode_One_Village_-_05.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Remains of Mos Espa in the Tunisian desert.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Campania_Caserta3_tango7174.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="747" height="236" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Campania_Caserta3_tango7174.jpg/220px-Campania_Caserta3_tango7174.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Campania_Caserta3_tango7174.jpg/330px-Campania_Caserta3_tango7174.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Campania_Caserta3_tango7174.jpg/440px-Campania_Caserta3_tango7174.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Campania_Caserta3_tango7174.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Reggia Di Caserta (Caserta, Italy) was the location for the Naboo Royal Palace.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Filming began on June 26, 1997, and ended on September 30 of that year, primarily taking place at Leavesden Film Studios in England. Leavesden was leased for a two and a half years so the production company could leave the sets intact and return after <a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">principal photography</a> had been completed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199953_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199953-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> The forest scenes on Naboo were filmed at <a href="/wiki/Cassiobury_Park" title="Cassiobury Park">Cassiobury Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Watford" title="Watford">Watford</a>, Hertfordshire.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starwars_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-starwars-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starwarslocations_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-starwarslocations-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pick-up_(filmmaking)" title="Pick-up (filmmaking)">Pick-ups</a> were shot between August 1998 and February 1999 after Lucas screened a rough cut of the film for friends and colleagues in May 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999137.E2.80.93138_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999137.E2.80.93138-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of the action and stunts were filmed by <a href="/wiki/Roger_Christian_(filmmaker)" title="Roger Christian (filmmaker)">Roger Christian</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Second_unit" title="Second unit">second unit</a>, which worked alongside the main unit instead of afterwards because of the high number of shots to be completed daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mak_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-mak-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Tunisian desert was again used for the Tatooine scenes;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Episode1_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Episode1-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Mos Espa was built outside the city of <a href="/wiki/Tozeur" title="Tozeur">Tozeur</a>. On the night following the third day of shooting in Tozeur, an unexpected sandstorm destroyed many of the sets and props. The production was quickly rescheduled to allow for repairs and was able to leave Tunisia on the date originally planned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-War_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-War-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The Italian <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Caserta" title="Palace of Caserta">Caserta Palace</a> was used as the interior of the Theed City Naboo Palace;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Episode1_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Episode1-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> it was used as a location for four days after it had been closed to visitors. Scenes with explosions were filmed on replica sets in Leavesden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199957_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199957-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A binder with the film's storyboards served as a reference for live-action filming, shots that would be filmed in front of a <a href="/wiki/Chroma_key" title="Chroma key">chroma key</a> blue screen, and shots that would be composed using CGI. The sets were often built with the parts that would be required on screen; often they were built only up to the heights of the actors. Chroma key was extensively used for digital set extensions, backgrounds or scenes that required cinematographer <a href="/wiki/David_Tattersall" title="David Tattersall">David Tattersall</a> to seek powerful lamps to light the sets and visual effects supervisor <a href="/wiki/John_Knoll" title="John Knoll">John Knoll</a> to develop software that would remove the blue reflection from shiny floors. Knoll, who remained on set through most of the production, worked closely with Tatterstall to ensure that the shots were suitable to add effects later. The cameras were fitted with <a href="/wiki/Automatic_identification_and_data_capture" title="Automatic identification and data capture">data capture</a> models to provide technical data for the CGI artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199977.E2.80.9379.3B_84.E2.80.9385_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199977.E2.80.9379.3B_84.E2.80.9385-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Phantom Menace</i> was the final <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> film to be shot on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/35mm_film" title="35mm film">35mm film</a> until <i>Episode VII</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a></i>). Some scenes, mostly of elements filmed by the special effects team, were shot on high definition, digital video tapes to test the performance of digital recordings, which Lucas and McCallum considered the next logical step because of the amount of digitizing—an expensive process compared to recording directly on digital media—for the compositing of computer-generated effects. All future films would be shot using <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> <a href="/wiki/CineAlta" title="CineAlta">CineAlta</a> high-definition video cameras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199979.E2.80.9380.3B_120_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199979.E2.80.9380.3B_120-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Editing took two years; Paul Martin Smith started the process in England and focused on dialogue-heavy scenes. <a href="/wiki/Ben_Burtt" title="Ben Burtt">Ben Burtt</a>—who was also the film's <a href="/wiki/Sound_editor_(filmmaking)" title="Sound editor (filmmaking)">sound editor</a>—was responsible for action sequences under Lucas' supervision. <a href="/wiki/Non-linear_editing_system" title="Non-linear editing system">Non-linear editing systems</a> played a large part in translating Lucas' vision; he constantly tweaked, revised and reworked shots and scenes. The final sound mix was added in March 1999 and the following month the film was completed after the delivery of the remaining visual effects shots.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999135.E2.80.93137.3B_149_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999135.E2.80.93137.3B_149-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">Effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:27%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"Writing the script was much more enjoyable this time around because I wasn't constrained by anything. You can't write one of these movies without knowing how you're going to accomplish it. With CG at my disposal, I knew I could do whatever I wanted".</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;"> —George Lucas<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999105_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999105-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>About 1,950 of the shots in <i>The Phantom Menace</i> have visual effects. The scene in which toxic gas is released on the Jedi is the only sequence with no digital alteration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-time-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The work was so extensive that three visual effects supervisors divided the workload among themselves—John Knoll supervised the on-set production and the podrace and space battle sequences, <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Muren" title="Dennis Muren">Dennis Muren</a> supervised the underwater sequence and the ground battle, and <a href="/wiki/Scott_Squires" title="Scott Squires">Scott Squires</a>, alongside teams assigned for <a href="/wiki/Miniature_effect" title="Miniature effect">miniature effects</a> and character animation, worked on the lightsaber effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999106_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999106-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Until the film's production, many special effects in the film industry were achieved using miniature models, <a href="/wiki/Matte_(filmmaking)" title="Matte (filmmaking)">matte</a> paintings, and on-set visual effects—although other films had made extensive use of CGI. Knoll previewed 3,500 <a href="/wiki/Storyboard" title="Storyboard">storyboards</a> for the film; Lucas accompanied him to explain factors of the shots that would be practical and those which would be created through visual effects. Knoll later said that on hearing the explanations of the storyboards, he did not know how to accomplish what he had seen. The result was a mixture of original techniques and the newest digital techniques to make it difficult for the viewer to guess which technique was being used. Knoll and his visual effects team wrote new computer software, including <a href="/wiki/Cloth_modeling" title="Cloth modeling">cloth simulators</a> to allow a realistic depiction of the digital characters' clothing, to create certain shots. Another goal was to create computer-generated characters that could act seamlessly with live-action actors. While filming scenes with CGI characters, Lucas would <a href="/wiki/Blocking_(stage)" title="Blocking (stage)">block</a> the characters using their corresponding voice actors on-set. The voice actors were then removed and the live-action actors would perform the same scene alone. A CGI character would later be added into the shot to complete the conversation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VE_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-VE-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> Lucas also used CGI to correct the physical presence of actors in certain scenes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-time-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Practical models were used when their visuals helped with miniature sceneries for backgrounds, set extensions, and model vehicles that would be <a href="/wiki/3D_scanner" title="3D scanner">scanned</a> to create the digital models or filmed to represent spaceships and podraces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999115.E2.80.93124_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999115.E2.80.93124-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lucas, who had previously confronted problems with the props used to depict R2-D2, allowed ILM and the production's British special effects department to create their own versions of the robot. Nine R2-D2 models were created; one was for actor Kenny Baker to be dropped into, seven were built by ILM and featured two wheelchair motors capable of moving 440 pounds (200 kg), enabling it to run and be mostly used in stage sets, and the British studio produced a pneumatic R2-D2 that could shift from two to three legs and was mostly used in Tunisia because its motor drive system allowed it to drive over sand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-R2_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-R2-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Lucas originally planned to create many of the aliens with computer graphics, but those that would be more cost-effectively realized with masks and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animatronic" title="Animatronic">animatronics</a> were created by Nick Dudman's creature effects team. These included the Neimodians, background characters in Mos Espa, the Jedi Council, and the Galactic Senate. Dudman's team was told where the creatures would be required six months before principal photography begun, and they rushed the production. The Neimodian suits, which were originally intended as digital characters, were delivered one day before they would be required on set. Dudman traveled to Skywalker Ranch to see the original creatures that could be reused, and read the script for a breakdown of scenes with practical creatures, leaving only the more outlandish designs to be created using CGI.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199965.E2.80.9366_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan199965.E2.80.9366-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>To research for the podrace vehicles, the visual effects crew visited a jet aircraft junkyard outside <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a> and scavenged four <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> engines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-time-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Life-sized replicas of the engines were built and sent to Tunisia to provide reference in the film. Except for Jake Lloyd inside a hydraulically controlled cockpit and a few practical podracer models, the entire podracing scene—which the effects crew designed to be as "out of this world" as possible—is computer-generated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Episode1_56-2"><a href="#cite_note-Episode1-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999119.E2.80.93120_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBouzereauDuncan1999119.E2.80.93120-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace_(soundtrack)" title="Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace (soundtrack)">Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace (soundtrack)</a></div>
<p>As with previous <i>Star Wars</i> films, <i>Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace</i> '​s <a href="/wiki/Film_score" title="Film score">score</a> was composed and conducted by <a href="/wiki/John_Williams" title="John Williams">John Williams</a>. He started composing the score in October 1998 and began recording the music with the London Voices and <a href="/wiki/London_Symphony_Orchestra" title="London Symphony Orchestra">London Symphony Orchestra</a> at <a href="/wiki/Abbey_Road_Studios" title="Abbey Road Studios">Abbey Road Studios</a> on February 10, 1999. Williams decided to use electronic instruments such as <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesizers</a> to enhance the sound and choral pieces to "capture the magical, mystical force that a regular orchestra might not have been able to provide", and create an atmosphere that was "more mysterious and mystical and less military" than those of the original trilogy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-williams_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-williams-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> One of the most notable tracks is "<a href="/wiki/Duel_of_the_Fates" title="Duel of the Fates">Duel of the Fates</a>", which uses the chorus to give a religious, temple-like feel to the epic lightsaber duel. The track was made into a music video.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Music_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Music-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> While composing Anakin's theme, Williams tried to reflect the innocence of his childhood and to foreshadow his transformation into Darth Vader by using slight suggestions of "<a href="/wiki/The_Imperial_March" title="The Imperial March">The Imperial March</a>" in the melody.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-williams_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-williams-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film's soundtrack was released by <a href="/wiki/Sony_Classical_Records" title="Sony Classical Records">Sony Classical Records</a> on May 4, 1999. This album featured the score, which Williams restructured as a listening experience; it is not presented in film order and omits many notable cues from the film because of the space restriction of the compact disc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> A two-disc "Ultimate Edition" was released on November 14, 2000. The set features almost the entire score as it is heard in the film, including all of the edits and loops that were made for the sound mix.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes">Themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_sources_and_analogues" title="Star Wars sources and analogues">Star Wars sources and analogues</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Maul_Devil.png"><img alt="Heads and shoulders shot of a man wearing black robes. He is bald and has horns on his head, his face is covered in black and red tattoos, and his eyes are yellow." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="319" data-file-width="750" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Maul_Devil.png/325px-Maul_Devil.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Maul_Devil.png/488px-Maul_Devil.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4a/Maul_Devil.png/650px-Maul_Devil.png 2x" width="325"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Maul_Devil.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The face of Darth Maul drew upon depictions of the Devil.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like previous <i>Star Wars</i> films, <i>The Phantom Menace</i> makes several references to historical events and films that George Lucas' watched in his youth. The <i>Star Wars</i> films typically mix several concepts from different mythologies together.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myth_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-myth-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Jedi practice <a href="/wiki/Zen" title="Zen">Zen</a>-like meditation and <a href="/wiki/Martial_arts" title="Martial arts">martial arts</a>, as did the ancient Japanese <a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">Samurai</a> warriors. The name "Qui-Gon" adapts the term <a href="/wiki/Qigong" title="Qigong">Qigong</a>, which refers to a Chinese discipline involving meditation and cultivation of the flow of the vital energy called "<a href="/wiki/Qi" title="Qi">Chi" or "Qi"</a> for healing, health and combat. The words <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ch%27i" title="Ch'i">Ch'i</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a>), <i>ki</i> (<a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a>) and the Indian term "<a href="/wiki/Prana" title="Prana">Prana</a>" all refer to the energy that is thought to flow through all living things, from the source of all chi (or power) which is "The Way" or "The <a href="/wiki/Tao" title="Tao">Tao</a>" in Chinese philosophy. In <a href="/wiki/Taoism" title="Taoism">Taoist</a> philosophy, from The Way, <a href="/wiki/Yin_and_yang" title="Yin and yang">yin and yang</a>—the opposing but complementary aspects of reality or nature—are born. Unlike Chinese philosophy, in which yin and yang are not moral qualities, the ancient Persian philosophy of <a href="/wiki/Zurvanism" title="Zurvanism">Zurvanism</a> taught that the dualism of dark and light forces are locked in an eternal battle while being two sides (or evolutes) of the same "Force", the force of time itself (Zurvan)—the prime mover. These elements derive primarily from <a href="/wiki/Eastern_religions" title="Eastern religions">Eastern</a> and Iranian religions and myths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myth_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-myth-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>There are many references to Christian beliefs in the film, such as the appearance of Darth Maul, whose design draws heavily from traditional depictions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_teaching_about_the_Devil" title="Christian teaching about the Devil">Christian Devil</a>, complete with red skin and horns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myth_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-myth-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Maul's facial tattoos were inspired by the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Brazil" title="Indigenous peoples in Brazil">indigenous peoples of Brazil</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vision_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-vision-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Star Wars</i> film cycle features a similar Christian narrative involving Anakin Skywalker; he is the "chosen one"—the individual prophesied to bring balance to the Force—who was conceived of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miraculous_birth" title="Miraculous birth">virgin birth</a> and is tempted to join the Sith. Anakin's fall from grace seemingly prevents him from fulfilling his destiny as the "chosen one". The inspiration behind the story of the virgin birth parallels a concept developed by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Campbell" title="Joseph Campbell">Joseph Campbell</a> and his work on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hero_with_a_Thousand_Faces" title="The Hero with a Thousand Faces">The Hero with a Thousand Faces</a></i>, which heavily influenced Lucas' writing of the original <i>Star Wars</i> trilogy's outline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-myth_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-myth-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_film" title="Japanese film">Japanese films</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Akira_Kurosawa" title="Akira Kurosawa">Akira Kurosawa</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hidden_Fortress" title="The Hidden Fortress">The Hidden Fortress</a></i> the original <i>Star Wars</i> film; scholars<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2014)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> say that <i>The Phantom Menace</i> was likewise influenced by Japanese culture. Film historians Geoff King and Tanya Krzywinska write, "The costume and make-up designs ... favour a mixture of the gothic and the oriental over anything very futuristic. The gothic is most strongly apparent in Darth Maul's demonic horns and the red and black make-up mask that borrows from the facial designs found in depictions of Japanese demons". King and Krzywinska say that "Qui-Gon's pony tail and Obi-Wan's position of apprentice further encourage a reading in terms of the Samurai tradition". The also say "Amidala, in keeping with her status and character, has a number of highly formal outfits ... to go with hair sculpted into a curve that frames make-up of a Japanese cast".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The release of the first new <i>Star Wars</i> film in 16 years was accompanied by a considerable amount of attention.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Few film studios released films during the same week as the release of <i>The Phantom Menace</i>; <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks" title="DreamWorks">DreamWorks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Universal_Studios" title="Universal Studios">Universal Studios</a> released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Love_Letter_(1999_film)" title="The Love Letter (1999 film)">The Love Letter</a></i> on May 21 and <i><a href="/wiki/Notting_Hill_(film)" title="Notting Hill (film)">Notting Hill</a></i> on May 28, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Love Letter</i> was a commercial failure but <i>Notting Hill</i> fared better and followed <i>The Phantom Menace</i> closely in second place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Employment consultant firm <a href="/wiki/Challenger,_Gray_%26_Christmas" title="Challenger, Gray &amp; Christmas">Challenger, Gray &amp; Christmas</a> estimated that 2.2 million full-time employees missed work to attend the film, resulting in a <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$293 million</span> loss of productivity. According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>, so many workers announced plans to view the premiere that many companies closed on the opening day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Queue areas formed outside cinema theaters over a month before ticket sales began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>More theater lines appeared when it was announced that cinemas were not allowed to sell tickets in advance until two weeks into the release. This was because of a fear that family theater-goers would be either unable to receive tickets or would be forced to pay higher prices for them. Instead, tickets were to be sold on a first-come-first-served basis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> However, after meetings with the <a href="/wiki/National_Association_of_Theatre_Owners" title="National Association of Theatre Owners">National Association of Theatre Owners</a>, Lucasfilm agreed to allow advance ticket sales on May 12, 1999, provided there was a limit of 12 tickets per customer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> As a result, some advance tickets were sold by <a href="/wiki/Ticket_resale" title="Ticket resale">scalpers</a> at prices as high as <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$100</span> apiece, which a distribution chief called "horrible" and said it was exactly what they wanted to avoid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Daily Variety</i> reported that theater owners received strict instructions from Lucasfilm that the film could only play in the cinema's largest auditorium for the first 8–12 weeks, no honor passes were allowed for the first eight weeks, and they were obliged to send their payments to distributor 20th Century Fox within seven days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Despite worries about the film being finished on time, two weeks before its theatrical release Lucasfilm preponed the release date from May 21 to May 19, 1999. At the ShoWest Convention, Lucas said the change was intended to give the fans a "head start" by allowing them to view it during the week and allowing families to view it during weekends. Foreshadowing his future conversion to <a href="/wiki/Digital_cinematography" title="Digital cinematography">digital cinematography</a>, Lucas said the film would be released on four digital projectors on June 18, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Eleven charity premieres were staged across the United States on May 16, 1999; receipts from the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> event, where corporate packages were available for between <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$5,000</span> and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$25,000</span>; proceeds were donated to the <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Glaser_Pediatric_AIDS_Foundation" title="Elizabeth Glaser Pediatric AIDS Foundation">Elizabeth Glaser Pediatric AIDS Foundation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> Other charity premieres included the <a href="/wiki/Dallas" title="Dallas">Dallas</a> premiere for the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Medical_Center_(Dallas)" title="Children's Medical Center (Dallas)">Children's Medical Center</a>, the Aubrey Fund for Pediatric Cancer Research at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial_Sloan-Kettering_Cancer_Center" title="Memorial Sloan-Kettering Cancer Center">Sloan-Kettering Hospital</a> in New York, the <a href="/wiki/Big_Brothers_Big_Sisters_of_America" title="Big Brothers Big Sisters of America">Big Brother/Sister Association</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philadelphia,_Pennsylvania" title="Philadelphia, Pennsylvania">Philadelphia</a> premiere, and the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_National_Medical_Center" title="Children's National Medical Center">Children's National Medical Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington, D.C.</a> A statement said that tickets were sold at <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$500</span> apiece and that certain sections of the theaters were set aside for disadvantaged children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
