<p>Lucasfilm spent <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$20 million</span> on the film's advertising campaign and made promotional licensing deals with <a href="/wiki/Hasbro" title="Hasbro">Hasbro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lego" title="Lego">Lego</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yum!_Brands" title="Yum! Brands">Tricon Global Restaurants</a>, and <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> Lucasfilm also helped the <i>Star Wars</i> fan club to organize an event called <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Celebration" title="Star Wars Celebration"><i>Star Wars</i> Celebration</a>, which was held in <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a>, Colorado between April 30 and May 2, 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teaser_trailer" title="Teaser trailer">teaser trailer</a> was released on selected screens accompanying <i><a href="/wiki/A_Bug%27s_Life" title="A Bug's Life">A Bug's Life</a></i> on November 17, 1998, and media reported that people were paying full admission at theaters to see the trailer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> A second trailer was released on March 12, 1999, with the film <i><a href="/wiki/Wing_Commander_(film)" title="Wing Commander (film)">Wing Commander</a></i>. Again, many fans paid full theater admission to watch the new trailer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> A bootlegged version of the preview was leaked to the Internet the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bootleg_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-bootleg-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The next morning, the trailer was released on the film's official website and shortly afterwards the servers became overloaded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> The theatrical trailer caused even more media attention because it was premiered in theaters and screened at the |ShoWest Convention in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> and was aired on <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Tonight" title="Entertainment Tonight">Entertainment Tonight</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Access_Hollywood" title="Access Hollywood">Access Hollywood</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bootleg_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-bootleg-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The teaser <a href="/wiki/Film_poster" title="Film poster">poster</a>, featuring Anakin with his shadow forming Darth Vader's silhouette, was released on November 10, 1998. After Lucas opted for a drawn theatrical poster, <a href="/wiki/Drew_Struzan" title="Drew Struzan">Drew Struzan</a>, the artist responsible for the Special Edition posters, was commissioned to illustrate, and the poster was unveiled on March 11, 1999. Lucasfilm dictated that, contractually, Struzan's illustration was the only art the foreign distributors could use, and other than the text, it could not be modified in any way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Many tie-in adaptations, such as a <a href="/wiki/LucasArts" title="LucasArts">LucasArts</a> <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace_(video_game)" title="Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace (video game)">video game</a> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a> and <a href="/wiki/PC_game" title="PC game">PC</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_I_(pinball)" title="Star Wars Episode I (pinball)">pinball machine</a> by <a href="/wiki/WMS_Industries" title="WMS Industries">Williams</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> a four-part comic book adaptation by Dark Horse Comics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> and a junior novelization by <a href="/wiki/Scholastic_Corporation" title="Scholastic Corporation">Scholastic</a> were released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace_(novel)" title="Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace (novel)">official novelization</a> was written by <a href="/wiki/Terry_Brooks" title="Terry Brooks">Terry Brooks</a>, who met with Lucas before writing the book and receiving his approval and guidance. It included information about pending developments in the following two installments of the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/General_Mills" title="General Mills">General Mills</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brisk_(beverage)" title="Brisk (beverage)">Brisk</a> were promotional partners in North America for the 2012 3D re-release but promotion was limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was extensively promoted in Japan; promotional products were sold by <a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domino%27s_Pizza" title="Domino's Pizza">Domino's Pizza</a>, Pepsi and Gari-Gari Kun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kellogg%27s" title="Kellogg's">Kellogg's</a> promoted the film internationally,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> and French restaurant <a href="/wiki/Quick_(restaurant)" title="Quick (restaurant)">Quick</a> launched three <i>Star Wars</i>-themed burgers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> Lucasfilm also partnered with <a href="/wiki/Variety,_the_Children%27s_Charity" title="Variety, the Children's Charity">Variety, the Children's Charity</a> to raise funds for children through the sale of a special edition badge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yoda_DVD_BD.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="446" data-file-width="512" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/88/Yoda_DVD_BD.png/250px-Yoda_DVD_BD.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/88/Yoda_DVD_BD.png/375px-Yoda_DVD_BD.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/88/Yoda_DVD_BD.png/500px-Yoda_DVD_BD.png 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yoda_DVD_BD.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Comparison between the puppet of Yoda, present in the theatrical and DVD releases, and the computer-generated model, present in the Blu-ray Disc and 3D releases.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The film was released worldwide on <a href="/wiki/VHS" title="VHS">VHS</a> between April 3 and 8, 2000. Two versions were released in North America on April 4—a standard <a href="/wiki/Pan_and_scan" title="Pan and scan">pan and scan</a> version and a <a href="/wiki/Widescreen" title="Widescreen">widescreen</a> Collector's Edition version. In its first two days of availability, the regular version sold 4.5 million copies and the limited edition sold 500,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> It was the first <i>Star Wars</i> film to be officially released on <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a>, on October 16, 2001. The special features included seven deleted scenes completed specifically for the DVD, a commentary track featuring Lucas and producer Rick McCallum, and several documentaries—including a full-length documentary entitled "The Beginning: Making Episode I". <i>The Phantom Menace</i> became the fastest selling DVD ever in the U.S.; 2.2 million copies were sold in its first week after release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The DVD version was re-released in a prequel trilogy box set on November 4, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> A <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laserdisc" title="Laserdisc">Laserdisc</a> version of <i>The Phantom Menace</i> was released in Japan several months before it was available on DVD in the U.S.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i>Star Wars</i> films were released on <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> on September 16, 2011;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Phantom Menace</i> was restored to improve the picture quality and remove the magnification present on the previous DVD release, restoring approximately 8 percent of the picture to the frame.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> In the Blu-ray release of <i>The Phantom Menace</i>, the Yoda puppet was replaced with a CGI model, making it consistent with the other films of the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars#Prequel_trilogy" title="Star Wars">prequel trilogy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="3D_re-release">3D re-release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 3D re-release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Phantom_Menace_3D.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="472" data-file-width="295" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/39/The_Phantom_Menace_3D.jpg/200px-The_Phantom_Menace_3D.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/39/The_Phantom_Menace_3D.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/39/The_Phantom_Menace_3D.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Phantom_Menace_3D.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Poster for the 3D re-release of <i>The Phantom Menace</i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On September 28, 2010, it was announced that all six films in the series would be stereo-converted to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3-D_film" title="3-D film">3D</a>. These would be re-released in episode order, beginning with <i>The Phantom Menace</i>, which was released to cinemas in February 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Prime_Focus_Limited" title="Prime Focus Limited">Prime Focus Limited</a> did the conversion under close supervision by ILM.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the 3D re-releases of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_II:_Attack_of_the_Clones" title="Star Wars Episode II: Attack of the Clones">Star Wars Episode II: Attack of the Clones</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_III:_Revenge_of_the_Sith" title="Star Wars Episode III: Revenge of the Sith">Star Wars Episode III: Revenge of the Sith</a></i> were postponed after Lucasfilm was bought by <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">The Walt Disney Company</a>, which decided to focus on the development of <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>George Lucas stated the 3D re-release was "just a conversion" of the film's 2011 Blu-ray release and no additional changes were made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> Only a change to Anakin's magnetic wand during the podrace scene—its tip was sharpened to more accurately fit the original 2D photography to the new 3D image—was confirmed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film received generally mixed reviews. As of 2014, <i>The Phantom Menace</i> holds a 57% "Rotten" rating on the review aggregator website <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, with an average rating of 5.8/10 based on 191 reviews, with the critics consensus: "Lucas needs to improve on the plot and character development, but there's plenty of eye candy to behold."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> It also has a score of 51 out of 100 ("mixed or average reviews") on <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a> based on 36 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> On both sites, it is the lowest-rated film in the <i>Star Wars</i> film series, excluding the animated feature <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Clone_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars: The Clone Wars (film)">Star Wars: The Clone Wars</a></i>. Many aspects of the scripting were criticized, especially that of the character Jar Jar Binks, who was regarded by many members of the older fan community as <a href="/wiki/Toyetic" title="Toyetic">toyetic</a>—a merchandising opportunity rather than a serious character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JarCNN_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-JarCNN-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Kenneth Turan of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> described Binks as "a major miscue, a comic-relief character who's frankly not funny." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> George Lucas criticized the American media for using fan opinions from the Internet as a reliable source for news stories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2002, with the release of <i>Attack of the Clones</i>, Ewan McGregor said he thought <i>The Phantom Menace</i> was "kind of flat", and said, "I think there is much more humor and ... color in 'Episode II'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> Drew Grant of <i>Salon.com</i> wrote, "Perhaps the absolute creative freedom director George Lucas enjoyed while dreaming up the flick's 'comic' relief—with no studio execs and not many an independently minded actor involved—is a path to the dark side." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-salon.com_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-salon.com-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Conversely, <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> gave it three-and-a-half stars out of four and called it "an astonishing achievement in imaginative filmmaking", and said "Lucas tells a good story." Ebert also wrote that "If some of the characters are less than compelling, perhaps that's inevitable" because it is the opening film in the new trilogy. He concluded his review by saying that rather than <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">Star Trek</a></i> films, filmmakers could "[g]ive me transparent underwater cities and vast hollow senatorial spheres any day."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> Owen Gleiberman of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> rated the film a B and complimented Liam Neeson's performance and the action scenes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> In an <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> review for the DVD release, Marc Bernardin gave the film a C-, calling it "haplessly plotted, horribly written, and juvenile".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> ReelViews.net's <a href="/wiki/James_Berardinelli" title="James Berardinelli">James Berardinelli</a> wrote;</p>
<blockquote>
<p>Looking at the big picture, in spite of all its flaws, <i>The Phantom Menace</i> is still among the best "bang for a buck" fun that can be had in a movie theater. It isn't as fresh as the original <i>Star Wars</i> nor does it have the thematic richness and narrative complexity of <i>The Empire Strikes Back</i>, but it is a distinct improvement over <i>Return of the Jedi</i>. In fact, after <i>Return of the Jedi</i>, I didn't have a burning desire to return to this galaxy 'far, far away', but, with <i>The Phantom Menace</i>, Lucas has revived my interest. Now, it's with genuine regret that I realize the next segment of the series is three long years away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnston_(critic)" title="Andrew Johnston (critic)">Andrew Johnston</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_Out_(magazine)" title="Time Out (magazine)">Time Out New York</a></i> wrote, "Let's face it: no film could ever match the expectations some have for 'Episode I – The Phantom Menace'. Which isn't to say it's a disappointment: on the contrary, it's awesomely entertaining, provided you accept it on its own terms ... Like the original film, it's a Boy's Own adventure yarn with a corny but irresistible spiritual subtext. The effects and production design are stunning, but they always serve the story, not the other way around."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Susan Wloszczyna of <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> said the film did "plenty right" and praised the characters Darth Maul and Watto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> David Cornelius of efilmcritic.com said the film's better moments "don't merely balance out the weaker ones—they topple them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> Colin Kennedy of <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine said that despite problems with pacing and writing "there is still much pleasure to be had watching our full-blown Jedi guides in action." He praised the visuals and Liam Neeson's performance, and said the duel between Darth Maul and the Jedi was "the saga's very best lightsaber battle".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Empire</i> magazine ranked <i>The Phantom Menace</i> on its list of "500 Greatest Movies Of All Time",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> and <a href="/wiki/Comcast" title="Comcast">Comcast</a> included the film on their lists of the worst movie sequels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> James Berardinelli wrote, "<i>The Phantom Menace</i> was probably the most overhyped motion picture of the last decade (if not longer), and its reputation suffered as a result of its inability to satisfy unreasonable expectations."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> William Arnold of the <i><a href="/wiki/Seattle_Post-Intelligencer" title="Seattle Post-Intelligencer">Seattle Post-Intelligencer</a></i> agreed that the film's massive hype caused many of the negative reactions, saying "it built expectations that can't possibly be matched and scuttled [the] element of storytelling surprise." He also said the film was "well made and entertaining" and was much better than similar box office fare released around that year, such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mummy_(1999_film)" title="The Mummy (1999 film)">The Mummy</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Matrix" title="The Matrix">The Matrix</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The introduction of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Force_(Star_Wars)#Force-sensitivity" title="Force (Star Wars)">midi-chlorians</a>—microscopic organisms that mediate use of the Force—in the film has been controversial among fans. Some viewed it as a concept that negates the Force's spiritual quality, although the film still portrays the Force as a mysterious entity using the midi-chlorians to communicate with living beings. Film historian Daniel Dinello says, "Anathema to <i>Star Wars</i> fanatics who thought they reduced the Force to a kind of viral infection, midi-chlorians provide a biological interface, the link between physical bodies and spiritual energy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Religion expert <a href="/wiki/John_D._Caputo" title="John D. Caputo">John D. Caputo</a> writes, "In the 'Gospel according to Lucas' a world is conjured up in which the intractable oppositions that have tormented religious thinkers for centuries are reconciled ... The gifts that the Jedi masters enjoy have a perfectly plausible scientific basis, even if its ways are mysterious: their bodily cells have a heavier than usual concentration of 'midi-chlorians'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the film's release, there was controversy over whether several alien characters reflect <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_stereotype" title="Ethnic stereotype">racial stereotypes</a>. For example the oafish, slow-witted Jar Jar Binks had long droopy ears reminiscent of dreadlocks and spoke with what many perceived as a Caribbean <a href="/wiki/Patois" title="Patois">patois</a> reminiscent of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jamaican_Creole" title="Jamaican Creole">Jamaican Creole</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> The greedy and corrupt <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Star_Wars_races_(K-O)#Neimoidian" title="List of Star Wars races (K-O)">Neimoidians</a> of the Trade Federation spoke with East Asian accents and the unprincipled trader Watto has been interpreted as a <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jewish</a> stereotype reminiscent of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a>' character <a href="/wiki/Fagin" title="Fagin">Fagin</a>. Lucas has denied all of these implications;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JarCNN_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-JarCNN-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> however, animator <a href="/wiki/Rob_Coleman" title="Rob Coleman">Rob Coleman</a> said he viewed footage of <a href="/wiki/Alec_Guinness" title="Alec Guinness">Alec Guinness</a> as Fagin in <i><a href="/wiki/Oliver_Twist_(1948_film)" title="Oliver Twist (1948 film)">Oliver Twist</a></i> to inspire his animators in the creation of Watto.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> One critic described Jar Jar Binks as "[s]ervile and cowardly ... a black minstrel-ish stereotype on par with <a href="/wiki/Stepin_Fetchit" title="Stepin Fetchit">Stepin Fetchit</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-salon.com_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-salon.com-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Eric_Dyson" title="Michael Eric Dyson">Michael Eric Dyson</a>, professor of <a href="/wiki/African-American_studies" title="African-American studies">African-American studies</a> at <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a>, said the entire Gungan people seem oddly suggestive of a primitive African tribe. Dyson said, "The leader of Jar Jar's tribe is a fat, bumbling buffoon with a rumbling voice, and he seems to be a caricature of a stereotypical African tribal chieftain."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-edition.cnn.com_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-edition.cnn.com-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office_performance">Box office performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Box office performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite its mixed critical reception, <i>The Phantom Menace</i> was a financial success, breaking many <a href="/wiki/Box_office" title="Box office">box office</a> records in its debut. It broke <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_World:_Jurassic_Park" title="The Lost World: Jurassic Park">The Lost World: Jurassic Park</a></i> '​s records for the largest single-day gross for taking more than <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$28 million</span> in the opening day and fastest to gross <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$100 million</span> in five days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> It also became the quickest film to reach the <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$200 million</span> and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$300 million</span> marks, surpassing <i><a href="/wiki/Independence_Day_(1996_film)" title="Independence Day (1996 film)">Independence Day</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Numbers_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Numbers-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Phantom Menace</i> was 1999's most successful film, earning <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$431,088,295</span> in North America and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$493,229,263</span> in other territories, taking <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$924,317,558</span> worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Numbers_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-Numbers-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> At that time, the film was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">third-highest-grossing film in North America</a> behind <i>Titanic</i> and <i>Star Wars</i>, and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">second-highest-grossing film worldwide</a> behind <i>Titanic</i> without adjusting for inflation of ticket prices. When adjusted for ticket price inflation, it ranked as the 19th-highest-grossing film domestically, making it the fourth <i>Star Wars</i> film to be in the Inflation-Adjusted Top 20. Outside North America, the film grossed over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10 million</span> in Australia (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$25.9 million</span>), Brazil (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$10.4 million</span>), France and Algeria (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$43 million</span>), Germany (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$53.9 million</span>), Italy (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$12.9 million</span>), Japan (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$109.9 million</span>), Mexico (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$12 million</span>), Spain (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$25 million</span>), and the United Kingdom and Ireland (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$81.9 million</span>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After its 3D re-release in 2012, the worldwide box office gross exceeded <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1 billion</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billion_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-billion-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> Although in the intervening years the film had lost some of its rankings in the lists of highest-grossing films, the 3D re-release returned it to the worldwide all-time top ten for several months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> In North America, its revenues overtook those of the original <i>Star Wars</i> as the saga's highest grossing film when not adjusting for inflation of ticket prices, and is currently the fifth-highest-grossing film in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> In North America its ranking on the Adjusted for Ticket Price Inflation list climbed to 16th place—one place behind <i>Return of the Jedi</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> The 3D re-release, which premiered in February 2012, earned <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$43 million</span>—<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$$22.5 million</span> of which was in North America—worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3D_opening_weekend_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-3D_opening_weekend-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> As of June 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the 3D re-release has earned US$102,727,119 worldwide—including $43.5 million in North America—and has increased the film's overall box office takings to <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$474.5 million</span> domestically, and <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$552.5 million</span> in other territories.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starwars3dgross_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-starwars3dgross-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's earnings exceeded <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$1 billion</span> worldwide on February 22, 2012, making it the first <i>Star Wars</i> film and the eleventh film in history—excluding inflation—to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billion_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-billion-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starwars3dgross_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-starwars3dgross-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>The Phantom Menace</i> was nominated for three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Editing">Best Sound Editing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound" title="Academy Award for Best Sound">Best Sound Mixing</a> (<a href="/wiki/Gary_Rydstrom" title="Gary Rydstrom">Gary Rydstrom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Johnson_(sound_engineer)" title="Tom Johnson (sound engineer)">Tom Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shawn_Murphy_(sound_engineer)" title="Shawn Murphy (sound engineer)">Shawn Murphy</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Midgley" title="John Midgley">John Midgley</a>); all of which went to <i>The Matrix</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oscars2000_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oscars2000-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> The film received seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award" title="Golden Raspberry Award">Golden Raspberry Award</a> (Razzie) nominations for <a href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award_for_Worst_Picture" title="Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Picture">Worst Picture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award_for_Worst_Director" title="Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Director">Worst Director</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award_for_Worst_Screenplay" title="Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Screenplay">Worst Screenplay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award_for_Worst_Supporting_Actor" title="Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Supporting Actor">Worst Supporting Actor</a> (Jake Lloyd as Anakin), <a href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award_for_Worst_Supporting_Actress" title="Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Supporting Actress">Worst Supporting Actress</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sofia_Coppola" title="Sofia Coppola">Sofia Coppola</a> as Saché), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Raspberry_Award_for_Worst_Screen_Couple" title="Golden Raspberry Award for Worst Screen Couple">Worst Screen Couple</a> (Jake Lloyd and Natalie Portman), and Jar Jar Binks actor <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Best" title="Ahmed Best">Ahmed Best</a> won the Worst Supporting Actor category.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> The film won <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award" title="Saturn Award">Saturn Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Costume" title="Saturn Award for Best Costume">Best Costumes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Special_Effects" title="Saturn Award for Best Special Effects">Best Special Effects</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Movie_Award" title="MTV Movie Award">MTV Movie Award</a> for Best Action Scene,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> and a <a href="/wiki/Young_Artist_Award" title="Young Artist Award">Young Artist Award</a> for Jake Lloyd's performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> It was also nominated for—among others—the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">BAFTAs</a> for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Special_Visual_Effects" title="BAFTA Award for Best Special Visual Effects">Visual Effects</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Sound" title="BAFTA Award for Best Sound">Sound</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Score_Soundtrack_for_Visual_Media" title="Grammy Award for Best Score Soundtrack for Visual Media">Best Score Soundtrack for Visual Media</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

(2005). <a class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/?id=W1oyiL-Je6MC" rel="nofollow">"Anticipation: The Real Life Story of Star Wars: Episode I-The Phantom Menace"</a>. iUniverse. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-595-34732-0" title="Special:BookSources/0-595-34732-0">0-595-34732-0</a>.</span><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AStar+Wars+Episode+I%3A+The+Phantom+Menace&amp;rft.au=Bowen%2C+Jonathan+L.&amp;rft.aufirst=Jonathan+L.&amp;rft.aulast=Bowen&amp;rft.btitle=Anticipation%3A+The+Real+Life+Story+of+Star+Wars%3A+Episode+I-The+Phantom+Menace&amp;rft.date=2005&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3DW1oyiL-Je6MC&amp;rft.isbn=0-595-34732-0&amp;rft.pub=iUniverse&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
